  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c3528572-bf18-4344-b923-dfa32e26c0cb'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/24209928-justin"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/24209928-justin">Justin</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
Neil Gaiman is one of the editors and writes the introductions to the stories, but has no pieces in the collection. There are no illustrations.
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_74173974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74173974" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Wallace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1142024-elizabeth-wallace"><img alt="Elizabeth Wallace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536676925p2/1142024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74173974?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Wallace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Wallace" href="/user/show/1142024-elizabeth-wallace">Elizabeth Wallace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061008337" href="/book/show/92061.The_Sandman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1142024-elizabeth-wallace?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74173974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2903062418728715823">I recently grabbed this book off my shelf, intending to just reread my favorite story "An Extra Smidge of Eternity" by Robert Rodi. And somehow ending up rereading the whole thing. I'm AMAZED at how much I'd forgotten from the last time I read it, because they're certainly not forgettable. I think I had as much fun reading this as I did the very first time I read it.<br/><br/>"Splatter" by Will Shetterly is pretty disturbing, but it's wonderful for all of us who wanted to hear just a teeny bit more about </span>
  <span id="freeText2903062418728715823" style="display:none">I recently grabbed this book off my shelf, intending to just reread my favorite story "An Extra Smidge of Eternity" by Robert Rodi. And somehow ending up rereading the whole thing. I'm AMAZED at how much I'd forgotten from the last time I read it, because they're certainly not forgettable. I think I had as much fun reading this as I did the very first time I read it.<br /><br />"Splatter" by Will Shetterly is pretty disturbing, but it's wonderful for all of us who wanted to hear just a teeny bit more about the "Cereal Convention" from "A Doll's House." (The answer to the question "Do cereal collectors eat their collection?" has got to be my favorite line in the whole story.) "Masquerade and High Water" is wonderfully sweet, "Each Damp Thing" is great for getting your heart racing, "The Mender of Broken Dreams" gives you a great look at how the Dreaming works (love the little details about fixing the dream of a tapestry) and Stopp't Clock Yard is just amazing in its style and quirky humor. Every single author in this book did an AMAZING job, and how many anthologies have you read where you can say that?</span>
  <a data-text-id="2903062418728715823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_52453819" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52453819" />
    <a title="PurplyCookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie"><img alt="PurplyCookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415491715p2/2214498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52453819?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PurplyCookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PurplyCookie" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie">PurplyCookie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=sandman-library">sandman-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=mythic-fiction">mythic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52453819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11736145051808655962">For eight years, Gaiman mined this rich vein, only to stop at the height of the series' popularity, at a point in time when he felt the story he had in mind from the beginning had reached its natural conclusion. Gaiman's creations live on however, in DC's new series <b>"The Dreaming"</b>, and in this anthology, written by several mainstream (i.e., non-comic book) writers. <br/><br/>Of Morpheus, from the Preface by Frank McConnell: <i>"He is not a god; he is older than all the gods, and is their cause. He is the hum</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11736145051808655962" style="display:none">For eight years, Gaiman mined this rich vein, only to stop at the height of the series' popularity, at a point in time when he felt the story he had in mind from the beginning had reached its natural conclusion. Gaiman's creations live on however, in DC's new series <b>"The Dreaming"</b>, and in this anthology, written by several mainstream (i.e., non-comic book) writers. <br /><br />Of Morpheus, from the Preface by Frank McConnell: <i>"He is not a god; he is older than all the gods, and is their cause. He is the human capacity to imagine meaning, to tell stories: an anthropomorphic projection of our thirst for mythology. And as such, he is both greater and less than the humans whose dreams he shapes, but whose thirst, after all, shapes him. As Titania would say, he does not exist; and thus he is all that matters." </i><br /><br /><br /><b>Masquerade and High Water - Colin Greenland </b> &gt;&gt; Provide insights into the backstage workings of The Endless, specifically that of the Pavilion of Recurrence. <br /><br /><b>Chain Home, Low - John M. Ford </b> &gt;&gt; What happened to those affected by Morpheus' disappearance during the time he was held captive in Burgess' basement? I almost skipped this story since it seemed to take forever to read. <br /><br /><b>Stronger than Desire - Lisa Goldstein </b> &gt;&gt; What is stronger than desire--is it love? What follows is a story about Desire and his/her human lover in so long a time, and of a wager between them. Included is a possible explanation of the origin of courtly love. <br /><br /><b>Each Damp Thing - Barbara Hambly </b> &gt;&gt; A scary piece featuring Cain and Abel. Cain unearths a mirror that Morpheus had hidden away for a pretty good reason.<br /><br /><b>The Birth Day - B. W. Clough </b> &gt;&gt; Wherein Morpheus visits a storyteller (the New Meeter of the band) who may just be too clever for her own good. <br /><br /><b>Splatter - Will Shetterly </b> &gt;&gt; A horror writer probably would have preferred to be guest of honor somewhere other than the Cereal Convention. Set at the infamous Serial Killers Convention as seen in <b>"The Doll's House"</b>. <i>"The world always made promises. Maybe he should see what the world delivered."</i>. <br /><br /><b>Seven Nights in Slumberland - George Alec Effinger </b> &gt;&gt; A delightful tribute to both <b>The Sandman </b>and <b>Little Nemo </b>.<br /><br /><b>Escape Artist - CaitlÃ­n R. Kiernan </b> &gt;&gt; A take on the childhood days of Wanda, nee Alvin, Mann, whose first appearance was in the story arc <b>"A Game of You"</b>. Having parents who exemplifies religious guilt is one of the worst ways to find out about who you truly are. <br /><br /><b>An Extra Smidgen of Eternity - Robert Rodi </b> &gt;&gt; <i>"Stories are important. They're all we've got, really. Stories are hope. They take you out of yourself for a bit, and when you get dropped back in, you're different--you're stronger, you've seen more, you've felt more. Stories are like spiritual currency."</i><br /><br /><b>Endless Sestina - Lawrence Schimel </b> &gt;&gt; For the sheer accomplishment of it. (Note: A sestina is a classical verse form, six verses of six lines each, in which the final words recombine according to an obvious formula from stanza to stanza.)<br /><br /><b>The Writer's Child - Tad Williams </b> &gt;&gt; Is a finely crafted story about loyalty and the value of innocence set against the backdrop of Dream or the Player King recognizing it. It reminds me of Lyta Hall--of the dreamstuff invading the waking world. <br /><br /><b>The Gate of Gold - Mark Kreighbaum </b> &gt;&gt; <i>"Even the Endless must dream."</i> A story of a doll's courage to save his charge from the nightmares that plagues her every night, as a manifestation of her ugly family life.<br /><br /><b>A Bone Dry Place - Karen Haber </b> &gt;&gt; An appearance of Despair, <i>"She is one of the Endless, sworn to duty here until the universe ends or her elder sister takes over."</i><br /><br /><b>The Witch's Heart - Delia Sherman </b> &gt;&gt; Featuring a she-wolf with a human shadow, a Eitch and a Lady (Desire playing yet again one of his/her games) for the quest to retrieve the witch's heart. <br /><br /><b>The Mender of Broken Dreams - Nancy A. Collins </b> &gt;&gt; One of the denizens of The Dreaming is The Mender, one repairs and restores dreams so they can be re-used from one dreamer to the next. Morpheus speaks of The Dreaming as such:<i>"Every human born has the keys to my kingdom within them. For many the Dreaming is simply a place to escap[e the pressures of being mortal. For a handful of poets and madmen it is the land of portents, signs, and inspiration. But for others, it is the one place where true happiness can be found; where beggars ride as kings, the spurned find love, the hungry feast." </i><br /><br /><b>Ain't You 'Most Done? - Gene Wolfe </b> &gt;&gt; What if you were born but you simply have never dreamed? How would it be like for a person to never experience the wonders and horrors of dreaming and nightmares? <br /><br /><b>ValÃ³sÃ¡g and Ã‰let - Steven Brust </b> &gt;&gt; This one reads very much a leaf from <b>"Brothers Grimm Fairytales"</b> but is no less wonderful. How do you trap the powers of Death &amp; Dream?<br /><br /><b>Stopp't-Clock Yard - Susanna Clarke </b> &gt;&gt; A tale that could easily have been part of the <b>"World's End" </b>story arc from the original series. (Gaiman himself comments <i>"I wish I had written this story."</i>) Clarke tells the amusing tale of magician Isaac Trismegistus and rogue John Paramore, a pair who invade Morpheus' realm to bring the deceased back to their loved ones. Morpheus is rendered perfectly, a distracted deity, swift to anger, but patient in the extreme. Dream waits out his tormentors, only to have his revenge stolen away by one of his siblings.<br /><br /><b>Afterword: Death - Tori Amos </b> &gt;&gt; A lyrical meditation on Death by songwriter Tori Amos close the anthology on a strong note (incidentally, this is also the introduction she wrote for <b>"Death: The High Cost of Living"</b>). On describing Death:<i>"She keeps reminding me there is change in the 'what is' but change cannot be made till you accept the 'what is'."</i><br /><br /><br />Although the stories are uniformly well crafted, they fail to break any new ground or provide novel insights into the rich cast of familiar characters. Most of the writers here seem content pursuing themes Gaiman has already visited rather than developing their own.<br /><br /><br /><u>Book Details: </u><br /><br /><u>Title</u> The Sandman: Book of Dreams (Signed)<br /><u>Author</u> Edited by Neil Gaiman &amp; Ed Kramer<br /><u>Reviewed By</u> Purplycookie</span>
  <a data-text-id="11736145051808655962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_269518928" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/269518928" />
    <a title="Kris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1401304-kris"><img alt="Kris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532285640p2/1401304.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/269518928?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kris" href="/user/show/1401304-kris">Kris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1401304-kris?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269518928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13304602738509166893">A mixed bag, to be honest. There were some real winners, like Robert Rodi's "An Extra Smidgen of Eternity" and Delia Sherman's "The Witch's Heart". It was nice to see Susannah Clarke's story as well; I started reading her work because Neil Gaiman had said in an interview that she was an author he enjoyed. I didn't care for Lawrence Schimel's "Endless Sestina", but I don't, as a rule, like a lot of poetry. According to wikipedia, several other authors (including Harlan Ellison, Jane Yolen, Charle</span>
  <span id="freeText13304602738509166893" style="display:none">A mixed bag, to be honest. There were some real winners, like Robert Rodi's "An Extra Smidgen of Eternity" and Delia Sherman's "The Witch's Heart". It was nice to see Susannah Clarke's story as well; I started reading her work because Neil Gaiman had said in an interview that she was an author he enjoyed. I didn't care for Lawrence Schimel's "Endless Sestina", but I don't, as a rule, like a lot of poetry. According to wikipedia, several other authors (including Harlan Ellison, Jane Yolen, Charles de Lint, Martha Soukup, Karawynn Long, and Michael Berry) had originally signed up to contribute to the anthology, but dropped out due to some confusion between the contracts DC Vertigo was giving people, and what the anthology's editors had originally promised them. Pity, I would have loved to have seen what Yolen and de Lint would have done with Morpheus. (This also explains Gaiman's dedication page in the edition I read, apologizing to the above writers.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13304602738509166893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Philip Shade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38325442-philip-shade"><img alt="Philip Shade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419542984p2/38325442.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3528628676?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Philip Shade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Philip Shade" href="/user/show/38325442-philip-shade">Philip Shade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061008337" href="/book/show/92061.The_Sandman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3528628676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4624756696745693494">Since finishing the original run of <i>The Sandman</i> there have been countless Sandman stories written by almost as many authors. But before the <i>The Dreaming</i> or <i>Sandman Universe</i> spun tales inspired by Neil Gaiman's Jungian archetype there was <br/><i>The Sandman: Book of Dreams</i>. It is the first collection of Sandman stories authored by anyone but Gaiman and set the tone for what would be the post-Gaiman Sandman universe that is still expanding 25 years later. <br/><br/>Like any anthology different <i>Book of Dreams</i> autho</span>
  <span id="freeText4624756696745693494" style="display:none">Since finishing the original run of <i>The Sandman</i> there have been countless Sandman stories written by almost as many authors. But before the <i>The Dreaming</i> or <i>Sandman Universe</i> spun tales inspired by Neil Gaiman's Jungian archetype there was <br /><i>The Sandman: Book of Dreams</i>. It is the first collection of Sandman stories authored by anyone but Gaiman and set the tone for what would be the post-Gaiman Sandman universe that is still expanding 25 years later. <br /><br />Like any anthology different <i>Book of Dreams</i> authors will appeal to different readers. Some of them are explicitly spinoff from, or fill in parts, of the original series. Other stories are dreams unto themselves; with only foundational reference to Gaiman's tales. <br /><br />I don't think any reader will give every story 5-stars, but I think that every fan will find a 5-star story, or three, between these covers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4624756696745693494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3471591992151727282" style="display:none">Like most anthologies, this is a mixed bag, i.e. some stories are better than others. However, even the best don't measure up to the standards of the <i>Sandman</i> comics, so I don't recommend it; at the very least, it's a book to borrow rather than buy.<br /><br />My favourite story is "Splatter" (by Will Shetterly), set during <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25101.The_Sandman__Vol__4_Season_of_Mists" title="The Sandman, Vol. 4 Season of Mists by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sandman, Vol. 4: Season of Mists</a>. If we ignore morality, and just look at it pragmatically, that's a prudent decision. Similarly, he changed his mind when they discovered an undercover journalist: I can understand his motivation for doing that, and they drove away from the hotel first. However, in this story they deliberately intended to kill at least two people on stage, i.e. inside the hotel. That weakens the original story, since he's saying "Don't kill anyone. Well, except for him. And those two. And maybe that other guy too. But nobody else!" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_773906412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/773906412" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1777325-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413646019p2/1777325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/773906412?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/1777325-julia">Julia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1777325-julia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer773906412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14679816802376186472">This is a collection of 18 stories by various authors (not Gaiman himself) who have written their pieces based on Gaiman's great concept of the Endless and of Morpheus, the Sandman, the King of Dreams. I only found two of them to be compelling--hence the three stars. But the two stories themselves are 5 stars for each. These two were the only ones to really bring the Dreaming World into the tale. <br/><br/>Barbara Hambly uses Gaiman's Cain and Abel to compose a chilling story called "Each Damp Thing", whe</span>
  <span id="freeText14679816802376186472" style="display:none">This is a collection of 18 stories by various authors (not Gaiman himself) who have written their pieces based on Gaiman's great concept of the Endless and of Morpheus, the Sandman, the King of Dreams. I only found two of them to be compelling--hence the three stars. But the two stories themselves are 5 stars for each. These two were the only ones to really bring the Dreaming World into the tale. <br /><br />Barbara Hambly uses Gaiman's Cain and Abel to compose a chilling story called "Each Damp Thing", where Morpheus must use all his powers to confront the evil Cain has unleased. He is so angry with Cain that he is poised to obliterate him--but Abel pleads for his brother's life, even though he knows they are doomed to repeat their own story forever. <br /><br />The best one for me is "The Mender of Broken Dreams" by Nancy A. Collins. When the Mender learns who he really is, that moment is the best in the book imho.<br /><br />I can't imagine anyone "getting" this book unless they are truly fans of the Sandman graphic novels, which have enchanted and haunted me for years. I suppose one could do the inevitable "googling" and get the background of the Endless--but the story is so much more intricate that that. <br /><br />Thank you to Hambly and Collins for enriching the Dream King and his castle for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14679816802376186472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2714524878" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2714524878" />
    <a title="Boethia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85593447-boethia"><img alt="Boethia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547064168p2/85593447.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2714524878?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Boethia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Boethia" href="/user/show/85593447-boethia">Boethia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2714524878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8742366262240747913">As with (almost) every anthology, this collection is somehow unbalanced. I basically didn't care for any of the stories from the first half of the book and I've enjoyed a fair bit of the second half - so I guess there's a balance in a sense, although this is entirely subjective.<br/><br/>The stories are of course connected by theme (sometimes very loosely, but the majority of them feature Morpheus or his siblings) and they're all within the same genre, which was to be expected, but to be honest, I'd welco</span>
  <span id="freeText8742366262240747913" style="display:none">As with (almost) every anthology, this collection is somehow unbalanced. I basically didn't care for any of the stories from the first half of the book and I've enjoyed a fair bit of the second half - so I guess there's a balance in a sense, although this is entirely subjective.<br /><br />The stories are of course connected by theme (sometimes very loosely, but the majority of them feature Morpheus or his siblings) and they're all within the same genre, which was to be expected, but to be honest, I'd welcome more diversity/experimentation. Not saying every short story was the same, but they weren't that different either; although each author had their own specific style and take on the dream realm, there wasn't anything that would hugely stand out, which ultimately leads to the unavoidable - juxtaposing the stories with Gaiman's own writing, which of course makes them a bit pale in comparison. It's almost as if the authors were too afraid to diverge from the lore, which is another reason why it's such a shame Harlan Ellison didn't contribute in the end, as he surely wouldn't treat Sandman as untouchable, and would write something jaw-dropping (for better or worse). <br /><br />Finally, my favourites: <i>Splatter</i> (serial killer convention from the Doll House p. II), <i>Escape Artist</i> (Alvin's/Wanda's backstory which I can pretty well imagine as being canon), <i>The Witch's Heart</i> (dark and heartbreaking Brothers Grimm type of fairy-tale).</span>
  <a data-text-id="8742366262240747913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1062810272" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1062810272" />
    <a title="Miles Ford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32758370-miles-ford"><img alt="Miles Ford" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1062810272?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miles Ford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miles Ford" href="/user/show/32758370-miles-ford">Miles Ford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1062810272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10752656497929024328">The Sandman: Book of Dreams<br/><br/>Neil Gaiman<br/><br/>The Sandman: Book of Dreams is a collection of the graphic novels by the name The Sandman. They are about a being named Dream. He is the master of dreams and can change anyoneâ€™s dream as he sees fit. He faces struggle when he is drawn from his kingdom and help captive for one hundred years by an organization wanting power. A side effect to Dream being held captive is that some people never wake up from their dreams.<br/><br/>I enjoyed the character Dream, or Morpheus,</span>
  <span id="freeText10752656497929024328" style="display:none">The Sandman: Book of Dreams<br /><br />Neil Gaiman<br /><br />The Sandman: Book of Dreams is a collection of the graphic novels by the name The Sandman. They are about a being named Dream. He is the master of dreams and can change anyoneâ€™s dream as he sees fit. He faces struggle when he is drawn from his kingdom and help captive for one hundred years by an organization wanting power. A side effect to Dream being held captive is that some people never wake up from their dreams.<br /><br />I enjoyed the character Dream, or Morpheus, because of the way he manages to achieve any goal without even lifting a finger. He has an air of power around him. He is interesting with the way he goes to achieve his goals, he usually threatens but never has to go through with the threats.<br /><br />A relationship I felt was important was the relationship between Dream and Death. When Dream has given up hope on finding one of his items of power Death convinces him that he should keep searching. When he is trapped in a prison in hell he calls on Death for help and she manages to free him. Without Death, Dream would've been stuck in hell or given up hope.<br /><br />One thing the book made me think about was the way a place in Dreamâ€™s kingdom becomes a real person and how he had to give up life to help restore balance and help the "mortals" live their lives. The thing I liked about this part was the way that he sacrificed himself to let others live. He did it without arguing and with no fuss. I thought it was a great show of selflessness.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the way this book was filled with many different stories but they all had an underlying story running throughout them. It all felt connected but not too focused on the one thing at all times. <br /><br />I also enjoyed the way parts of the stories were humorous and others were quite serious, with serious themes. I felt it made the book more enjoyable to read as after a very serious story it would most likely roll into quite a relaxed one with a laid back vibe to it.<br /><br />I would recommend this to anyone that enjoys Neil Gaiman's work or fans of more serious graphic novels.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10752656497929024328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_438370410" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/438370410" />
    <a title="Tara Hall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6826004-tara-hall"><img alt="Tara Hall" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442608455p2/6826004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/438370410?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tara Hall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tara Hall" href="/user/show/6826004-tara-hall">Tara Hall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer438370410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7719217412120093714">I have been a fan of Neil Gaiman since the 90s, and so when I saw this anthology of short stories based on his characters, I picked it up used. It took me a long time to read, as most of the stories were not ones that kept me on the edge of my seat. It also had been some time since I had read Sandman, and though I once had been familiar with the seven siblings Dream, Death, Desire, Despair, Destruction, Delirium, and Destiny, remembering them took about half the book.<br/>Anthologies are hard to rate</span>
  <span id="freeText7719217412120093714" style="display:none">I have been a fan of Neil Gaiman since the 90s, and so when I saw this anthology of short stories based on his characters, I picked it up used. It took me a long time to read, as most of the stories were not ones that kept me on the edge of my seat. It also had been some time since I had read Sandman, and though I once had been familiar with the seven siblings Dream, Death, Desire, Despair, Destruction, Delirium, and Destiny, remembering them took about half the book.<br />Anthologies are hard to rate. If I really like one story, I tend to let that overshadow the rest, and bump up the rating. However, the reverse is true for a bad story. This anthology had several of both kinds of stories, with a lot of stories that were decent, too.<br />There were of course some really fantastic stories, such as Splatter by Will Shetterly, about an author who gets access to a serial killer convention, Each Damp Thing by Baraba Hambly, about Cain and Abel's discovery of a monstrous thing that threatens to destroy The Dreaming, and The Gate of Cold, by Mark Kreighbaum, about a doll who goes in search of the Dream King to end his beloved human child's nightmares. These stories are worth buying the anthology to read and should not be missed. there were several other stories that were average and decent, too. However, there were twice as many stories that were not so good. They felt to me like dreams, with a lot of disconnects and things that didn't make that much sense. I also must give credit here to The Witch's Heart, which ranks as the single most terrible short story I have ever read in my life. This was not because this story was not well written, because is was well written. But it was the most depressing thing I have ever read, ever. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7719217412120093714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10085832149858224186" style="display:none">I don't know if the newer printed edition of this (paperback, and with a different cover) is in any way different from this edition (hardcover with a yellow and blue cover with a raven). Collins.</span>

    <a title="George" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4219638-george"><img alt="George" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337632911p2/4219638.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer854723766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4979150121975174205">Enjoyable, but not as good as the actual Sandman stories. A few of the stories here were great, but most felt to me like someone going out of their way to write a story about the Endless. Like the authors thought it would be cool and fun, but since they weren't their characters it was like wearing a pair of shoes that don't quite fit. Recommended for anyone that loved The Sandman, but if you haven't read those, this isn't a must-read (although you may actually like it better without knowing Gaim</span>
  <span id="freeText4979150121975174205" style="display:none">Enjoyable, but not as good as the actual Sandman stories. A few of the stories here were great, but most felt to me like someone going out of their way to write a story about the Endless. Like the authors thought it would be cool and fun, but since they weren't their characters it was like wearing a pair of shoes that don't quite fit. Recommended for anyone that loved The Sandman, but if you haven't read those, this isn't a must-read (although you may actually like it better without knowing Gaiman's stories). 3.5 stars on this for me...</span>
  <a data-text-id="4979150121975174205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('n2PZi1X54DS4R+DHwqEPKYcxwZ6hQkyny7SWXlnmYfhFP3Qbh04rSbS5frRwZ+NdlpxiilTMGROnMy6IyfD1qQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mRW/76+2KSP1/2B9hCOj1m76ZT+L6OhU7Zl9P7Gd+VhDSRJ/fQHiXvkB/g425U+if1fGK35mveCBHsXpIYttCQ==')})
  }
